## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic records stand beside the doctrine's own observability demands, sidecar supervision requires health checks, bounded startup waits, and log caps, setup lifecycle requires handing long-running work to owned supervised paths, channel progress makes long operations inherently visible, and updater configuration treats artifact provenance as an observable correctness property
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because desktop observability is supervision-shaped rather than telemetry-shaped, the app must watch its own children, sidecars, setup tasks, update flows, because no operator watches a user's machine
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: importing server observability, dashboards and centralized logs, misses the desktop inversion, the log cap rule exists because unbounded logs on user machines are a disk-space failure no operator will ever rotate
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: observability rules the doctrine mandates plus this node's own audit records, delivery-time log hygiene checks belong to the gates theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the four observable surfaces, sidecar health and logs, setup task ownership, channel-visible progress, and update provenance, each with its pattern anchor
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the log-cap requirement is the doctrine's most desktop-native observability rule, server doctrine says log more and rotate centrally while this file says cap at the source, because the observer is the user's finite disk, a complete inversion of the observability economics the system design theme teaches for services

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside the doctrine's performance stance, responsiveness is engineered structurally, async handlers for anything that can stall the UI, transport shape matched to payload, channels for volume, binary responses instead of JSON blobs, store payloads bounded, blobs out of band, and setup work bounded so startup never blocks the UI into oblivion
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine's performance rules all protect the same resource, the UI thread's responsiveness, because a desktop app's perceived quality is that thread's latency, not aggregate throughput
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: throughput-first reasoning misallocates effort, a fast bulk pipeline that stalls the UI during setup fails the user in the first second regardless of steady-state numbers
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the doctrine's structural performance rules, quantitative measurement method belongs to the system design theme's latency doctrine
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the five structural rules as the performance doctrine, each anchored to its pattern and phrased as protecting UI responsiveness
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the rules form a payload-size gradient, small structured data flows through store and events, sustained streams through channels, large binaries through binary responses and out-of-band files, so performance design here is a routing decision, matching each payload to its lane, rather than an optimization decision
